Negotiating Jin Army's Downsizing

▲ Generals' opinions are gradually converging

▲ But there are still no concrete measures

Taiyuan Correspondence: The long-troubled situation in Shanxi has recently seen the return of Xu Yongchang and Wang Jingguo, who have been mediating extensively. With the support of Song Zheyuan and Pang Bingxun, the headquarters meeting on the 27th was attended by all, and opinions were exchanged, showing a great willingness to compromise. According to the resolution of the headquarters meeting, it was originally scheduled to continue the meeting at the original site from the next day to study various detailed measures. However, since that meeting, various parties have gathered and discussed for several days, mostly in private residences or hotels. Yesterday morning around 9 o'clock, Shang Zhen, Xu Yongchang, and Yang Aiyuan went to the Shanxi Grand Hotel together to discuss with Ji Yiqiao, Chen Xingya, Hu Yiling, and others, and studied in detail the opinions put forward by the various army commanders. Finally, Shang Xu, Ji Hu, and others all believed that the army commanders' proposals should be formally reported to Deputy Commander Zhang, and Shang Zhen also expressed his willingness to relinquish the position of army commander. As for the army commanders' proposal to implement a ten-division system and reduce the total number of troops by one-third, Ji Hu and others intend to follow Deputy Commander Zhang's reply. This meeting lasted for four hours, and Shang Xu and others returned to their residences around 2 p.m. Although the exact results of the meeting are not very detailed, according to someone close to a certain army commander, the meeting of Shang Xu, Ji Hu, and others today was to discuss the results of the previous day's headquarters meeting in full, and to report the priorities to Deputy Commander Zhang. All the difficulties of the Jin-Sui army were also reported incidentally. The post-settlement of Jin-Sui is indeed closely related to today's meeting. At 6 p.m. last night, Xu Yongchang invited the nine army commanders to another discussion meeting at Sun Chu's private residence. Sun Chu, Yang Yaofang, Wang Jingguo, Li Shengda, Li Fuying, Yang Xiaoou, Yang Chengyuan, Zhang Huizhao, Feng Pengzhu, and others were all present. The steps for downsizing and post-settlement measures were discussed. Regarding the army's organizational system, Xu intends to reorganize the Jin army into five armies, each with a seven-regiment system, forming a total of thirty-five regiments. There is also a proposal to abolish the army commander system and organize a military committee, with each committee member responsible for managing military affairs. After much discussion, no satisfactory result was reached, and the nine army commanders still insisted on the clever telegram proposal, saying that by studying and implementing this principle, actual difficulties could be avoided, and the troops could be gradually demobilized, so as not to ruin the local area and harm the people. The results are still pending further discussion.

Ji Yiqiao and others' mission was originally to inspect. After the headquarters meeting the day before yesterday (27th), the meeting's situation was conveyed to Ji and others. It is said that Ji and others always wanted to maintain the Deputy Commander's decree and did not want to convey the matter to Zhang. Therefore, at yesterday's meeting at Sun's residence, it was heard that they planned to directly telegraph Zhang in the name of the generals and Xu Shang, stating the actual situation of the Jin-Sui armies, the difficulties in demobilization, the proceedings of the previous headquarters meeting, and the will of the generals, and requesting Zhang to start from reality. It is said that this telegram is currently being drafted, and once it is completed and agreed upon by all parties, it will be sent. (January 30th)

Yu-E-Wan Border Pacification Headquarters Moves to Hankou

▲ Li Mingzhong, Ji Hongchang, and Zhang Yinxiang have all arrived in Hankou

Hankou Correspondence: The Yu-E-Wan Border Pacification Commissioner's Office, originally located in Xinyang, has recently moved to Hankou for the convenience of command. After Commissioner Li Mingzhong and Director He of the Wuhan Branch exchanged telegrams, they designated the old Russian Consulate in Special District Two as the office site. Li first sent Ji Hongchang, the commander of the 22nd Route Army, and Zhang Yinxiang, the commander of the 31st Division, from Xinyang to Hankou to arrange everything. Ji and Zhang arrived in Hankou on January 31st. Li himself set off southward from Xinyang on the first of this month, leading Chief of Staff Wang Zhenhuai, Secretary-General Lu Hongtu, Adjutant-General Ge Jinzhang, Chief of Military Law Liu Guozhen, Chief of Management Miao Dianqi, and all the office staff. They arrived in Hankou on the morning of the 2nd and immediately began working. That evening, Director He and Xu Yuanquan and Liu Wendao hosted a banquet to welcome Li, and invited Wang Jinyu, Ji Hongchang, Xia Douyin, Zhang Yinxiang, and others to accompany them. During the banquet, Li reported to Director He on the bandit suppression in the Yu border area and discussed the current large-scale bandit communists who are disrupting the E East area. It was generally decided that Xia Douyin and Ji Hongchang's troops would still be stationed in E East as the main force for bandit suppression. Ge Yunlong's troops would leave the Yu border area to Huang'an, and Pan Shanzhai's troops would leave the Wan border area to Qishui, attacking the bandits' flanks. A large-scale joint suppression will be carried out within three or four days. After the banquet, everyone dispersed in joy. Today, the reporter separately interviewed Li, Ji, Zhang, and others and obtained their statements as follows:

▲ Li Mingzhong's speech briefly stated, "Since I was ordered to take charge of the pacification affairs of the border areas of the three provinces of Yu, Wan, and E, I have been following the plan formulated by the Commander-in-Chief, commanding the troops, and combining prevention and suppression, striving to eliminate the bandit communists in the shortest possible time, so that the people in the border areas of the three provinces can live and work in peace. All troops such as Ji Hongchang, Ge Yunlong, Zhang Yinxiang, etc., and Xia Douyin, Pan Shanzhai, etc., who are under my command, have all arrived at the designated locations. After I met with Director He, I have already discussed the border area pacification work once, and will implement it separately according to the original plan in the future. As for the situation in the border areas of each province, I will personally inspect them if necessary, so as to understand the situation in various places and supervise the troops to suppress them nearby."

▲ Ji Hongchang's speech briefly stated, "Since our division was ordered to take charge of bandit suppression, we have been stationed in southern Henan. Under the command of Commissioner Li, we have cleared out several small groups of scattered bandit communists. Recently, a large group of bandit communists from the Wan border area came from the Shangcheng area. After our division pursued them, the bandits injured two pseudo-division commanders and suffered more than 3,000 casualties. Our army also suffered more than 800 casualties and finally repelled them. However, the remaining bandits are still rampant. In addition to Shangcheng, there are still remnants of bandits in the Huangchuan and Guangshan areas. To completely annihilate them, it is necessary to have three divisions of troops to surround and suppress them. Commissioner Li is currently discussing thorough elimination methods with Director He of the Branch, and I have also reported to Director He on the joint suppression in the Yu-E border area. After a concrete plan is negotiated, I will return to defense to supervise the suppression."

▲ Zhang Yinxiang's speech briefly stated, "Although the main force of the communist bandits in northern Hubei has collapsed, they have not yet been eliminated. In the future, the clearing and suppression must be carried out with both military and political forces. Commissioner Li originally planned to convene a pacification conference in Xinyang to discuss concrete measures. However, he received a telegram from the Commander-in-Chief, instructing him to follow the second step of the plan for the pacification of the border areas of the three provinces of Yu, Wan, and E. Ji's troops and our division may be assigned the responsibility of pursuing and suppressing, while ordering friendly forces to defend and block. We vow to eliminate the bandits within the deadline. After I pay another visit to Commissioner Li, I will return to Songbu to take charge of clearing and suppressing." (February 3rd)

Rampant Banditry in Northern Guangdong's Lesser North River

▲ Li Mingrui's troops capture Lian County from Jianghua

▲ Local bandits in Lianshan and Xingzi and other areas are rising

Guangzhou Correspondence: Li Mingrui's communist army in southern Hunan has occupied Yongming, Jianghua, and other counties bordering the three provinces of Hunan, Guangxi, and Guangdong, and has caused great devastation. According to refugees who recently fled from Jianghua to Lianzhou, when the bandit news spread, the people were already in a state of panic. However, the defense force of the county seat was weak and dared not resist. Therefore, Li's troops drove straight into Jianghua County, established a Soviet puppet government in the city, with Li Mingrui as the chairman, and ordered the Red Army to capture landlords and capitalists. It was found that Li's troops entered the city on the 6th of the month, and began searching, arresting, burning, and killing on the 9th, resulting in hundreds of deaths in three days. All title deeds of land and industries owned by landlords and capitalists were confiscated and burned. Refugees are constantly on the road, with the majority seeking refuge in Lianshan. The people of Lian County felt even more apprehensive after hearing this, because Lian County is only three hundred li away from Jianghua, a three-day journey. Moreover, local bandits nearby are stirring, showing signs of responding to Li's troops. Therefore, in recent days, many people in Lian County have also fled to Yingde in the Northern River with their sons and daughters. According to news from the Yuehan Railway Bureau, refugees from Qinglian, Yangshan, and other areas below Lian County suddenly fled to Yingde Station on January 24. According to the refugees, after Li's bandits captured Jianghua, they took the road through Jianglan and captured Lianshan, splitting into two routes, one to peek into Lian County, and the other to Yangshan. At the same time, Deng Shixi and Huang Kun, local bandits in Lianshan and Lian County, took the opportunity to rise up. Therefore, Taipingxu below Lian County has also been occupied by bandits, and dozens of shops have been burned. Another part of Li's troops entered Guangdong from Jianghua's Baishimen, invading Lianshan. As a result, the communist bandit forces suddenly grew larger. Another part of Li's troops entered Xingzi Market, which borders Lian County and Lechang, via Dongpo from Jianglan. The Guangdong authorities have recently dispatched two aircraft from Kesai to fly to the Lian County area to scout for bandit traces. However, the weather has been bad for several days, and the valleys are filled with thick clouds, making it impossible to discern directions. They flew to the Yingde area and turned back. However, according to investigations, the various bandit forces seem to be divided into three routes to peep into the Greater and Lesser North Rivers of Guangdong Province. One force in Xingzi intends to rush out of Lechang and invade Shaozhou and Shixing. One force in Lian County intends to invade Gongruyuan and exit Longgui. One force in Lianshan intends to attack Yangshan, Qinglian, and Hankuang, and copy out of Yingde. As for Lian County, it was besieged by Li's troops on the 21st. Yesterday, the Pingshi Telegraph Bureau's urgent telegram reported on the 22nd, briefly stating that Lian County was besieged by Li Mingrui's troops on the Horse Day, and Xingzi was also occupied by Li's troops on the same day. On the morning of Horse Day, the telegraph lines in Lian County were cut off, and telegrams sent to Lian County by various telegraph bureaus could not be forwarded. The postal routes in Lian County were also impassable. According to reconnaissance reports, bandit traces were found in Yangshan County on the 24th. Since Yangshan is below Lian County, it can be known that Lian County has been captured by bandits if there are bandits in Yangshan. It was found that the Yangshan local bandits are only about 5,000 in number, and it is difficult for them to find food wherever they go. It is expected that when the government troops arrive to suppress them, it will not be difficult to wipe them out in one fell swoop. The Guangdong authorities are currently dispatching the 3rd Independent Regiment of Deng Hui to Ru Yuan to block and suppress them. The 3rd Teaching Regiment of Wang Dinghua and the newly compiled 16th Division's Supplementary Regiment of Liao Daoming are also heading from Yingde to Han Kuang to intercept them. The two regiments of Tan Langxing and Wu Jianxiong are also being transferred back from Xiongshi, with Wu's regiment going to Ru Yuan to assist in the suppression, and Tan's regiment going to Lechang Pingshi to guard against Xingzi and other places. Recently, the Guo Runhua Regiment of the 63rd Division was also transferred back to the province from Mengjiang, Guangxi, and transferred to the Lesser North River to assist the Wang Deng regiments in advancing and suppressing the Li bandits in Lianyang. It is also heard that Yan Yingyu's regiment will also be transferred back from Guizhou during the day to assist in the defense of the Northern River.

Jiangsu Province Establishes Village Clearance Headquarters

▲ Ye Chucang reports two missions

The Jiangsu Provincial Government, in accordance with the village clearance regulations promulgated by the central government, organized the Village Clearance Headquarters, and legally appointed the chairman of the provincial government as the director, the director of the civil affairs department as the deputy director, and the director of the security department as the affairs director. The staff of each department were transferred from various departments of the provincial government. The headquarters held its establishment ceremony at 9:00 a.m. yesterday (4th) in the auditorium of the provincial government. Lan Weibin, the representative of the Provincial Party Headquarters, Zhang Zhijiang, the Pacification Supervisor, Director He of the Provincial Government, and Director Li, and other guests and staff from various departments of the provincial government, about 300 people, attended. First, Chairman Ye Chucang led the ceremony and delivered an opening speech, briefly stating that the village clearance affairs in Jiangsu Province had been handled by the Department of Civil Affairs since August last year, but the work done could not be carried out as a whole due to the different situations in each county. Today, the establishment of the headquarters can actively carry out village clearance in various counties. The current plan is to order each county to submit the household registration investigation form, joint security form, and firearms inventory form to the headquarters for review within February as the first step. The second step of the work is to send personnel to conduct on-site investigations to address the ineffectiveness of village clearance in some counties and the concern that various counties may have filled out the forms inaccurately, so as to achieve the purpose of village clearance. Next, Lan Weibin, the representative of the Provincial Party Rectification Committee, gave a speech, generally stating that village clearance is the post-settlement work after pacification, and hoped that the government would list village clearance work as the policy direction for this year. Next, Zhang Zhijiang, the Pacification Supervisor, gave a speech, briefly stating that the people are the foundation of the state, and the foundation is solid and the state is peaceful. Village clearance is a way to secure the people and strengthen the foundation. The Jiangsu Provincial Government has a strong revolutionary spirit, and he believed that the village clearance work would definitely be completed soon. Next, Director He delivered a speech on behalf of the Provincial Government, briefly stating that the military is now pacified, and the whole province should carry out village clearance uniformly, identify the targets, determine the goals, and work towards them, which will surely be effective. Finally, Deputy Director Hu Pu'an gave a reply speech, and the meeting adjourned at 11:00 a.m. (5th)

Police Inspector Zhou Runshi Interrogated in Wuxi for Soliciting Prostitutes

Wuxi Correspondence: The case of Zhou Runshi, a police inspector of the Department of Civil Affairs, soliciting prostitutes and engaging in adultery with married women in Wuxi. Zhou was detained by the Department of Civil Affairs in Zhenjiang on the 3rd. It was originally scheduled to be escorted to this county the day before yesterday, but he had not arrived by evening. The details have been recorded in this newspaper. It is now learned that at 1:00 a.m. yesterday (5th), Director Hu of the Department of Civil Affairs sent two platoon leaders from the 2nd Battalion of the Guard Battalion to escort Zhou from Zhenjiang by car to Wuxi. He arrived in Wuxi at about 4:00 a.m. and temporarily stayed at the Liangxi Hotel. At 9:00 a.m., Zhou was escorted to the County Government. Then, County Magistrate Pan telephoned Xu, the director of the Public Security Bureau, ordering him to escort the persons involved in the case to the county for interrogation. After receiving the order, Director Xu immediately sent detectives to escort the plaintiff Shen Xiang and the three witnesses, Zhou Xingzhen, the concubine who had been prostituted by Zhou, and Wang Lihong, a local prostitute, to the county for questioning. At 11:30 a.m., County Magistrate Pan personally opened the court in Jingshu Hall for interrogation. Many people watched. After County Magistrate Shen took his seat, he used a vermilion pen to summon each person one by one for questioning. The interrogation was completed at 10:10 p.m. The statements of each person are recorded below:

Wang Lihong: Testified that she was 20 years old and has been a prostitute for two or three years. On the evening of the 4th, she accompanied Commissioner Zhou at No. 83 New World, introduced by Wang Chongxi, and stayed for three days, giving me 15 yuan. I met Zhou Chazhen at New World. I called New World on the evening of the 3rd and asked if Xingzhen was there. The waiter replied that she was at No. 83, so I went there and was introduced to Commissioner Zhou by Wang Chongxi.

Zhou Xingzhen: Testified that she was 20 years old and from Yixing. Commissioner Zhou was introduced by Wang Chongxi to stay in Wuxi for one night, and also stayed with someone surnamed Fang for one night. Later, I went to Suzhou with Commissioner Zhou and stayed for one night. The five yuan was given to me by the person surnamed Fang and transferred to Zhang Chongxi. At 6:00 p.m. on the 28th, I took a car to Suzhou to shop. Commissioner Zhou said he would go to Suzhou with me. We arrived in Suzhou at 7:00 p.m. and stayed at No. 80 Dongwu Hotel. We went out to watch a play and returned to the hotel at 11:00 p.m. and slept in the same bed. At 5:00 a.m., my husband, Shen Xi, took the police to the hotel. Then I went to the police station. Officer Wang questioned both my husband and me. Commissioner Zhou was not questioned. I don't know how it was resolved. I heard that Commissioner Zhou went to Wujiang. My husband and I returned to Wuxi. When I was at the Suzhou Bureau, Officer Wang persuaded my husband. My husband said yes.

▲ Shen Xiang: Testified that he was 20 years old. Zhou Xingzhen was taken in as a concubine in July of the 19th year. Xingzhen used to be a local prostitute and had been opening a room at New World for a long time. After I learned that she was sleeping in the same room with Commissioner Zhou, I went to the hotel to see. Because Zhou was a commissioner, I didn't dare to interfere. According to Xingzhen, she and Commissioner Zhou were from the same hometown and there was nothing else. Later, I went to New World. According to the waiter, Xingzhen and Commissioner Zhou had gone to Suzhou. So I went to Suzhou with my friend Qian Zhenxiang and others at 3:40 a.m. that night. We arrived in Suzhou at 5:00 a.m. Because there was a familiar waiter at Dongwu Hotel, we went to the hotel. We saw that the passenger card for No. 80 was Zhou Shi. Then we went to the door of the room to peek and heard Xingzhen singing in bed. We immediately reported to the police and knocked on the door of the hotel. Zhou Runshi opened the door wearing his clothes and went to the police station together. We transferred to the 2nd Sub-Bureau of the 3rd Branch. Officer Wang persuaded us to resolve it peacefully and told me to take her back and gave me 50 yuan for travel expenses and told me to make a statement. Zhou Runshi also said to me in person that he would give me 50 yuan. Later, we went to the Jingjiang Restaurant to eat. The 50 yuan was a roll of banknotes. I didn't receive it. All the gold bracelets, gold rings, gold watch chains, etc. that Zhou Xingzhen took away could not be determined whether they were taken out last time or this time.

▲ Zhou Runshi: Testified that he was 24 years old, from Yixing, and a graduate of the first class of the Police Academy. This time I came to Wuxi to sleep with Wang Lihong first, and then I was with Zhou Xingzhen. Wang Chongxi introduced me because Lihong and Xingzhen were always together. I stayed at No. 80 Dongwu Hotel in Suzhou. I didn't give 50 yuan to Shen Xiang at the branch. When I was at the Suzhou Branch, Officer Wang said that there was no evidence of abduction, but there was evidence of soliciting prostitutes, so he advised Shen Xiang to take Xingzhen back. After I saw the report in Shengze, I went to the school in Zhenjiang and then to the Department of Civil Affairs, ordering me to go to Wuxi. This matter has nothing to do with Qin Enrui.

At this point, County Magistrate Pan ordered Shen Xiang to go back and wait for the County Court to summon him, and ordered Zhou Runshi, although there was no evidence of abduction, but he was suspected, to wait to be dismissed. In the afternoon, he prepared a letter and transferred the three witnesses, Wang Lihong and Zhou Xingzhen, to the County Court for interrogation. After adjourning the court, County Magistrate Pan ordered the County Public Security Bureau to summon Wang Chongxi to the county and transfer him to the court for interrogation. That night, he reported the interrogation and other details to the Department of Civil Affairs for review. County Magistrate Pan had not transferred Zhou Runshi and others after interrogating them until 5:40 p.m.

▲ Shen Xiang (i.e., Shen Zanru) took Zhou Xingzhen as a concubine in mid-July last year. Soon after, the two sides disagreed and divorced with the mediation of Chen Lishi, Yu Qin, Ying Huamei, and others, and Shen Xiang gave 100 yuan to Zhou Xingzhen (i.e., Xu Shishi) to sever the relationship between husband and concubine. At that time, with the mediation, 100 yuan was given to Xu Shishi as travel expenses. After the separation, there must be no private gatherings or entanglement of money. Wuhu Quick Mail

▲ Wuhu's five inner customs gates have been repeatedly requested by the Anhui Provincial Chamber of Commerce to be abolished early. A provincial special tax bureau will be established in Wuhu, with 22 special tax branches in various counties. Li, the deputy tax commissioner of the Tianjin Customs, was previously sent to Wuhu to inspect and plan, and it is proposed to appoint Li as the director of the tax bureau. It will be realized in the near future.

▲ The Anhui Provincial Chamber of Commerce is sincerely afraid that the new tax rate will exceed the original Likin tax amount after the Ministry of Finance levied the new supplementary tax after the Likin tax was abolished, so it telegraphed the Ministry of Finance, requesting that national economy and people's livelihood be taken into account. The Ministry of Finance replied that the general outline and supplementary measures for business tax in various provinces have been submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and passed in various provinces. What the association said may be a misunderstanding. I hope to publicize the purpose of the Ministry to revitalize tax laws, so that we can all understand it.

▲ The six-corner passport fee for rice and grain exports levied by the Anhui Provincial Government,

After repeated efforts by Anhui merchants, it was finally agreed to reduce it by two corners, and the actual levy was four corners per stone. Rice merchants are still not satisfied, but because accumulated rice is in urgent need of export, it has been registered and exported at the Wuhu Provincial Rice Certificate Circulation Inspection Office. On the one hand, it is still appealing to the National Government. Today, the Provincial Chamber of Commerce has received an order from the Ministry of Finance, stating that it has been approved by the Executive Yuan to strictly order the Anhui Provincial Government to abolish the new rice certificate donation in order to comply with the original intention of Likin abolition. However, this matter is related to the military and political expenses of Anhui Province, so Governor Chen Diaoyuan has gone to Beijing yesterday to consult with the National Government on a solution.

▲ The 171st Brigade of the 57th Division stationed in Wuhu previously received an order from the Commander-in-Chief's Office, and a review class was immediately sent to Wuhu for inspection. It was recently learned that the inspection is now planned to be suspended or postponed. Therefore, Yue Shengxuan, the commander of the 57th Division stationed in the province, has decided to come to Wuhu for inspection himself on the 10th of this month. The military here is already preparing for it.

▲ According to reports, the Wuhu Public Security Bureau's Detective Team found that bandits were hiding in a Wang family in Rulin Street in the city. Local Correspondence

Songjiang

The planning to organize a cleaning office in Songcheng is making gradual progress. Last year, the First District Office and the County Public Security Bureau designed and planned to organize a cleaning office, dividing the whole city into six districts and soliciting merchants to contract. Later, the Department of Civil Affairs instructed that it was easy to cause monopoly and harm farmers, so it was not approved. Now, the director of the Public Security Bureau, Shen Jingyi, and the district chief of the First District, Zhong Taishi, have repeatedly discussed and re-submitted it to the County Government for instructions. It is heard that the County Government, after receiving the report, has copied the previous order of the Department of Civil Affairs and the reports submitted by the bureau and the district office, and sent them to the Health Movement Committee for reconsideration, and then submitted them to the County Political Conference for review.

A collection of bandit cases from various places. On the 21st of last month, a gang of bandits kidnapped six men and women, including Dr. Xie Zichun, in Jiangzhuang Town, Punan. At that time, it was said that they were shot down by the police team and all were rescued. This is actually a rumor. According to the report, the first to be kidnapped that day were a Shen family member, a girl who had just reached marriageable age, Zhang Zitang's five-year-old younger sister, and the daughter of the owner of Tan Yiji South Goods Store, all of whom lived in Zhang Heng's home. The police team stationed in the mountains was outnumbered, so they were allowed to escape. It is heard that people are now in contact, but none of the six are wealthy. Also, on the evening of the 3rd, more than ten bandits broke into the home of Zhu Anda in Zhangcunbang, 38th Map, Fifth Ward, and kidnapped Zhu Anda's children and nephews. They also entered the bedroom and robbed gold and silver ornaments, and burned all the title deeds they found, causing great losses. The whereabouts of the kidnapped people are currently unknown.

Suzhou

Bandit Activity Rampant Near Cheng Lake: In the Xidang Upper Village area of Yuanzhi Township, on the edge of Yangcheng Lake, which belongs to the county, a group of over ten lake bandits suddenly arrived around 8 PM the night before last. They robbed the home of villager Zhang Junbo and, upon leaving, abducted Zhang's four-year-old son, Sifu. Furthermore, the villages of Xu Wantou and Xi Jilou in the same township were also robbed by lake bandits the night before last, who also looted over ten shi of white rice from the Pu family.

Continued News of the Surrender of a Reactionary Offender: It was learned yesterday (the 5th) that Cao Qiheng, a woman from Jiangdu, had come to Suzhou with a friend the day before, and, realizing she had joined the Communist Party and regretting it, went to the High Court to surrender and request amnesty. The High Court Prosecutor Zhu Jun, because the day had already passed the office hours, was unable to hold a hearing. He then convened a hearing at 2 PM yesterday afternoon, and because the woman had expressed remorse and the circumstances were relatively minor, he instructed her to find someone to bail her out while the investigation was completed before further action was taken.

Qingpu

Fang Baolong and Grandson Abducted: At about 10 PM the night before last, the home of villager Fang Baolong in Xiaojing area of Sian Bridge Township was suddenly invaded by more than twenty bandits armed with iron rulers and wooden sticks. They broke down the door and abducted Fang Baolong and his grandson. After the abduction, they headed east.

Robbery Recorded: Su Desu, a Hunanese who lives near Tailai Bridge Town outside the South Gate, makes a modest living by cultivating Dangtian fields. The night before last, many bandits suddenly broke down the door and stole over fifty shi of rice, causing a loss of over a thousand yuan. Furthermore, the home of Wang Youliang in Yaogang area outside the East Gate was also visited by several bandits the night before last. They silenced the occupants and stole thirty-six shi of white rice, as well as clothing and ornaments worth hundreds of yuan.

Fengxian

Summoning a Large Number of River Workers: Since the audit of Nanshutang River project expenses was referred to the judiciary by the provincial government, the Zhenjiang Court summoned Jiang Rongchu and Zhang Fengtai, directors of the East and West River Bureaus of the project, for repeated interrogations. As a result, because the account books and receipts still needed to be verified, the court ordered the county to issue summons yesterday for Chen Shiqian and Jiang Duanfu, the accountants of the two projects, and more than twenty personnel involved, including Gu Renan and Tang Zixiong, to appear in court. A public hearing and judgment will be held on the afternoon of February 10. The plaintiffs, including Zhuang Tianmei, Xu Yizhou, Tang Baosheng, and Shen Baoming, as well as Zhuang Shiru and other members of the River Workers Committee, were also notified by the court to appear in court at the same time for questioning.

Wuxi

Fugitive from Xinghua Arrested in Wuxi: Liao Dajin, leader of the detective squad of the county police brigade, received a tip from an informant yesterday that Ji Mingzhang, a wanted fugitive for the murder of Zhao Shilin, a member of the Xinghua police team, was hiding at No. 74 Qiande Lane. Liao reported to Brigade Leader Wang, who led the detectives to arrest Ji Mingzhang on the spot. He was then sent to the brigade headquarters for interrogation.

Bidding Results for Vacant Land at Wuxi Station Announced: The Beijing-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration, in order to revitalize the market, specially ordered the real estate section of the bureau to plan the vacant land on both sides of Wuxi Station and invite bids for leasing it to build municipal houses. The bid boxes were sealed and sent to the Shanghai Administration on the 29th of last month. It is now learned that the bidding results have been announced, with the rental price being 36 yuan, 2 jiao, and 5 fen per mu.

Provincial Pawnbroking Representatives Go to the Provincial Government to Petition: The pawnbroking industry throughout Jiangsu Province, because of Article 16 of the new provincial regulations regarding redemption interest beyond one month, which concerns the principal, held a temporary provincial pawnbroking meeting at the Wuxi County Chamber of Commerce in December of last year, resolving to petition the ministry and the province to maintain the old regulations. The petition was rejected. The pawnbrokers in various counties then consulted by letter and telegram and unanimously agreed that the pawnbroking industry had become extremely weak in recent years. If the new provincial regulations on redemption interest beyond one month were followed, the pawnbrokers would be unable to survive. If the provincial government could not approve the maintenance of the old regulations, they would all report closures. Su Minsheng, Zhou Guren, Yao Diyuan, Pan Zhixi, Cao Junde, Qin Zhuoru, Qian Sunji, and others were appointed to go to the provincial government yesterday (the 4th) to gather and hold a temporary meeting. The representatives will go to the provincial government today (the 5th) to petition and personally deliver petitions. If the petition is still unsuccessful, they will petition to cancel the old regulations, where interest does not exceed five per month, and to not restrict pawnbrokers from reporting closures, in order to ensure business freedom and protect the principal.

Changshu

County Magistrate Opens Joint Defense Meeting: Nantong opened a joint defense meeting on February 5, attended by the county magistrates of Nantong, Haimen, Chongming, Qidong, Changshu, and the district head of the 4th Water Police District. Tan Yigui, the county magistrate of Changshu, took the Dada Company steamboat from Shanghai to Nantong on the 4th to attend the meeting. After the meeting, it was heard that he still had to go to Wuxi to attend the joint defense meeting and report important matters to the province in person.

Central Government Plans to Purchase the Iron Qin and Copper Sword Tower Collection: Books are related to a nation's culture and are of great importance. There are four major book collectors in our country: the Yang family of Shandong, the Ye family of Hunan, the Fan family of Zhejiang, and the Qu family of our county, whose Iron Qin and Copper Sword Tower. However, the collections of the first three families have been dispersed due to various calamities. Only the Qu family's collection in our county, starting with Qu Yong during the Qianlong and Jiaqing periods, has been preserved for more than two hundred years despite countless disasters. It is said that during the Hong and Yang rebellions, the Qu family wrapped the books in dozens of layers of oil paper and submerged them in water, but they were still damaged. When Duan Fang was the Governor of Jiangsu, he once considered purchasing them, but it did not happen. Now it is heard that the central government plans to purchase them with funds for national preservation. Cai Yuanpei of the former National Government and Zhang Zhongren, a gentry from Suzhou, once came to Changshu to negotiate with the Qu family. It is now heard that a special commissioner will be sent to negotiate with the owner of the Iron Qin and Copper Sword Tower regarding the collection of books.

Police and Bandits Clash Fiercely at Zhu Jing Bridge: Zhu Jing Bridge in the Fushan district is adjacent to Haikou and is a place where bandits often appear. Around 11 PM the night before last (the 2nd), more than ten bandit boats were docked near Zhu Jing Bridge in Haikou, planning to land and rob. Yu Changgen, a resident of the area, spotted them and rushed to Tangfang Bridge to report to the police squad. Squad Leader Guan immediately dispatched thirty squad members to the area and sent scouts ahead. The bandits gathered in the woods to discuss their plans, and the police opened fire and dispersed, charging into the woods. Seeing the police, the bandits also fired rifles wildly. After an hour of fierce fighting, more than ten bandits swam back to their boats and fled. The whereabouts of more than ten other bandits are unknown. On the night of the 3rd, two more bandit boats attempted to rescue the dispersed bandits, but fortunately the police were prepared and blocked their landing. The bandits retreated again.

Hostage from Maojia Bridge Oil Shop Released: Yao Shou, the owner, and Xue Yanxing, the clerk, of the Shentongshun Oil Shop in Maojia Bridge outside the North Gate of our county, were robbed and kidnapped on the 26th of last month. It is now heard that Yao and Xue have safely returned home. It is said that they were taken to the port, and after pleading bitterly, they were released. However, Yao has been secretive since returning to the town, and it is difficult for outsiders to meet him. The reason for this is unknown. The oil shop has been heavily in debt recently, and since the incident, creditors have been flocking to the Maojia Bridge shop to demand payment as the settlement period has expired, but Yao has never been seen.

Zhenjiang

District Office Meeting to Restore Rice Market: The Zhenjiang First District Office believes that Zhenjiang has no production and relies entirely on goods from other places. Since the rice market moved to Wu, the commercial center has become desolate. Although the provincial government has moved to Zhenjiang, the commercial center has not improved. If Zhenjiang is to be revitalized, the rice market must be restored. Therefore, the district chief convened a meeting of all town chiefs yesterday to set a date to invite key figures in the rice industry to jointly discuss solutions, and appointed Cao Liqing, Wan Zhongping, and Yin Keqin to contact the Party Headquarters and the Chamber of Commerce for all matters.

Nantong

Handling Inspection of All County Public and Private Firearms: With the bandits and communists in the county pacified, the military, political, and police agencies, in order to eliminate hidden dangers, ordered all districts by the county government to uniformly inspect public and private firearms starting from March 1, with a deadline of half a month to complete the inspection.

County Party Headquarters to Implement Reorganization: Many members of the Nantong County Party Headquarters have been transferred. Reorganization is now being implemented, with Chen Guanying elected as a standing committee member.

Zhang Zha Petitioning for Return of Property: Zhang Zha, a resident of the county, was accused of having evidence of colluding with the enemy when Sun Jun invaded the south in the 16th year. He was charged in the Special Criminal Court but has not appeared in court. The provincial government resolved to issue a warrant for his arrest and confiscate all of his property. Zhang has fled to Dalian. He has now hired lawyer Dong Kang to sue the Nantong County Court, requesting the return of his property. The petition was approved and submitted to the Jiangsu High Court for review.

Yangzhou

Tax Collection Methods Determined After the Yun Office Moves North: The Yun Office moved to Guanyun on the 1st of this month, and the Huaibei Yun Deputy has also moved to Yangzhou. Previously, there was talk about the issue of tax collection and shipping orders in Huaibei, and it was originally intended to be completely transferred to the Yangtze Salt Branch for handling. However, Director Wang strongly argued and submitted seventeen proposed methods to Finance Minister Song Yun, who approved them for implementation. Therefore, the current regulations stipulate that although the shipping orders are issued by the Yangtze Salt Branch, the name of the Lianghuai Yun Office is still used. Tax collection is also carried out according to these regulations. As for the allocation of salt, it seems to be within the scope of the branch chief and there are no problems. However, it is heard that Yun Commissioner Wang has not yet gone to Guanyun to confirm.

Gaoyou

Finance Bureau Specially Formulates Collection Methods: The Finance Bureau, due to the fact that major households in the city have delayed paying the grain tax, has specially formulated seven collection methods: (1) Order the grain scribes to detail the names and addresses of major households in the urban area and assign police to urge them to pay, holding the name cards of the county magistrate and the bureau chief, requiring a response on the same day without delay. (2) Issue summons and designate clerks Chen Zigang and Jia Huachun to check at all times, and if anyone exceeds the deadline without paying, immediately send them to the county government for arrest. (3) The police's urging of collection should be supervised by clerks Chen Zigang and Jia Huachun at all times, and no negligence is allowed. (4) Designate clerks Cao Jingzhe and Tian Lecheng to be in charge of selecting major households who have not paid and lead the police to their doors to compel them to pay. (5) The director or section chief will personally urge the particularly large households to pay. (6) Request the Public Security Bureau Police Team to send four or six police officers to the bureau every day to be dispatched. (7) The police team sent by the Public Security Bureau Police Team will be given four jiao of ocean (silver dollar) for food each day. The performance will be assessed by the middle of February, and if there are achievements, rewards will be given.

Education Bureau Section Chief Dismissed and Another Appointed: Yang Youqing, the general affairs section chief of the county education bureau, has been absent from his post for a long time. Director Sun has now dismissed him and appointed Gong Liujing to succeed him.

Two Factions of Bandits Clash in Gaoyou: Recently, due to unequal distribution of loot, the bandits in the Zhoujinhe area of the tenth district of the county have split internally. The leaders of the two factions are Yan Shucai, who is based in Yan Family Village of Baoyi, and Zhang, who is entrenched in Zhoujinhe of Youyi. Each faction has more than a hundred bandits. The two factions opened fire on each other for several hours the day before yesterday, and there were casualties on both sides. The animosity has deepened in recent days. Every night, they post sentries and fire guns to demonstrate their strength. Residents in the area are extremely frightened, and those with some assets have been moving away.

Jiaxing

Jiaxing-Haiyan Boundary Issue Resolved: The Wangdian District of Jiaxing borders Haiyan County, and the boundary is not clear. Citizens of Wangdian District requested the county government to jointly survey with the Haiyan County government to avoid disputes. Although the two counties sent personnel to jointly survey, the issue was unresolved for a long time due to various problems. Recently, Huang Weiqing and other resident representatives of the Southeast Village of Wangdian District telegraphed the county government, requesting that personnel be sent to re-survey as soon as possible to resolve the issue. The Haiyan and Jiaxing county governments drafted a compromise solution to include the original Southeast Village, etc. of Jiaxing County into the Shuangcun and Lucun of the Yan County of Haiyan County, and to include the Shuangcun and Lucun of the Yan County of Haiyan County into Jiaxing. Having obtained the consent of the local residents, the survey has been completed and the map has been submitted to the Department of Civil Affairs for review and approval.

Pinghu

Major Kidnapping Case Occurs in Guangchen Town: Guangchen Town, which is two or nine li away from Pinghu and is an important route from Pinghu to Xincang, was visited by ninety bandits around 10 PM on the third night. They advanced by land and water, each carrying guns and weapons. They first went to the Quan family in the south of the town to rob, and kidnapped Quan Rongsheng's son and Quan Guanchang's grandson. They then robbed Zhang Zhenxing's rice shop, the Wang family's butcher shop, and the Yuan family, and Zhang Zhenxing's daughter, Jian, and her daughter, Yun'e, were also kidnapped, as well as Yuan Adi's two sons. After robbing until 11 PM, they sent the six male and female hostages to the bandit boat that had been pre-stationed in the West Market and marched in formation to the northeast. When they reached Zhangjiafen in Shicun, they broke into the Xu family and kidnapped Xu Shunguan and Xu Baoquan as well.

Local News

Military Law Review Committee of the Garrison Command Releases Political Prisoners Yesterday

▲Qiu Luanxie and 12 Others

▲Sun Yizhang Dies in Prison from Illness

The Military Law Review Committee of the Songhu Garrison Command held its second review meeting from 1 PM to 4 PM yesterday afternoon at the Longhua Command Headquarters. Five committee members, Zhou Shida, Dai Yuanchuan, Liu Tongyi, Su Fuchou, and Zhong Huan, were present. They immediately decided to grant amnesty in ten political prisoner cases, totaling twelve people: Qiu Luanxie, Weng Chuqing, Gu Jintang, Fang Zheng, Sun Jishi, Peng Yifu, Chen Dazhou, Sun Jiu, Li Ruyi, Deng Heng, Zhang Bingtao, and Chen Shiqing. Among them, Qiu Luanxie is already 84 years old and is a skilled calligrapher. He was arrested in the French Concession in this city during the Yan-Feng War last year and is now specially pardoned and released. Chen Shiqing was originally convicted of counter-revolution and kidnapping. Yesterday, only his counter-revolution part of the charges was pardoned; the kidnapping part was not, so he still cannot regain his freedom. Others are detained in Nanjing, Suzhou, or in the Caohejing prison. Yesterday, official documents were sent to notify their release. As for Brigade Commander Sun Yizhang, a subordinate of Sun Chuanfang, who was decided to be pardoned last Thursday, it is now learned that he died long ago from illness in the Caohejing prison.

Aviation Plan of the Ministry of Transportation

▲16 Air Routes Established Nationwide

▲Eurasian and Beijing-Ping trial flights next month

▲Shanghai-Guangdong and Shaanxi-Gansu are being planned

A reporter from the New Voice Agency met with Li Jingzong and Lin Tianlan, section chiefs of the Aviation Department of the Ministry of Transportation, yesterday and inquired about the Ministry's recent facilities for aviation development. Mr. Li answered them one by one. The following is a separate record:

▲Aviation Plan: Mr. Li said that the Aviation Plan of the Ministry of Transportation divides into sixteen routes. The Shanghai-Chengdu line has already opened flights to Hankou, and will soon be extended to Yichang. Eurasian Aviation and Beijing-Ping Aviation will be able to conduct trial flights at the beginning of next month. As for Shanghai-Guangdong Aviation, it is in the planning stage. Two amphibious aircraft purchased for this line can be transported to Shanghai recently. In addition, the most important route is the Shaanxi-Gansu line, which has important relations in military and cultural affairs. The Ministry of Transportation is also planning and preparing for it. Departing from Nanjing, passing through Kaifeng, Zhengzhou, Luoyang, Tongguan, and entering Shaanxi and Gansu, it can be carried out as soon as there are economic resources.

▲Mail Distribution: In the past, European mail transported to China via Siberia had to take eighteen days to reach Shanghai, and even the fastest would take no less than sixteen days. After the opening of Eurasian Aviation in the future, European mail will only take four days to reach Shanghai. In the future, the distribution of mail will be as follows: Beijing-Ping Aviation, passing through Xuzhou, Jinan, Tianjin, and reaching Beiping from Nanjing, will specialize in transporting domestic mail. Eurasian Aviation will pass through Shanghai, Nanjing, Jinan, Beiping, Duolun, and reach Manchuria. Before China and Russia restore diplomatic relations, a joint transport method will be adopted. After leaving the country, it will be transferred by the Russian Aviation Company, passing through Irkutsk and reaching Moscow, and then by a company jointly formed by Germany and Russia to fly to Berlin. Because the Russians suddenly claim to be developing commerce, merchants and travelers are searched with great rigor, so passage is difficult.

Eurasian Company: The organization of the Eurasian Aviation Company has a board of directors at the highest level, with nine directors. The chairman of the board is Wei Yifu, and the vice chairmen are Shuang Qing and Schmidt. Among the six Chinese directors, there is still one vacancy, which is being filled. Below the board of directors is a general manager, and below him are three groups: Lin Tianlan and Feng Xike (manager of the German Siemens Foreign Firm) are the director and deputy director of the Finance Group; Schmidt is the director of the Machinery and Aviation Group; and Li Jingzong is the director of the Operations Group. The deputy director has not yet been determined. The various regulations will be discussed and determined after the trial flight. The headquarters is determined to be in Beijing, and the Shanghai office will be a Shanghai branch office. The Shanghai branch office was originally located at the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Transportation on Maigen Road. Because the location is remote, it is planned to move to the central district.

▲Foreign Personnel Arrive in Shanghai: The Eurasian Aviation Company has hired two pilots, five mechanics, and one commercial officer from the German Hansa Company. Yesterday (the 4th), they arrived in Dalian in two batches via Siberia and arrived in Shanghai by Dalian Maru and another ship. The first batch of purchased aircraft was originally scheduled to arrive on the 10th, but due to a slight delay en route, it will be extended to the 12th. The second batch of machinists will arrive at the beginning of March, and the second batch of aircraft will arrive on March 15. After the first batch of aircraft arrives in Shanghai, it will take about twenty days to assemble before the trial flight can be carried out. Whether the trial flight will be extended to Manchuria will depend on the equipment along the way.

▲Director Meeting: At 5:30 PM yesterday afternoon, Lin Tianlan, director of the Finance Group of Eurasian Aviation Company, Li Jingzong, director of the Operations Group, and Schmidt, director of the Machinery and Aviation Group, convened a joint meeting of directors to discuss various preparatory matters and the relocation of the Shanghai office, as well as other important issues. The meeting adjourned after a long time. The reporter asked whether the China Aviation Corporation was liable for compensation for the Shanghai plane crash in which passengers died with the plane. Mr. Li said that aviation in all countries has insurance, but our country, being newly established, lacks it. Because the aviation company stipulates that it is not responsible for passengers' luggage, the company cannot be responsible for compensation. Because the other party demands a large amount of compensation, the company will inevitably go bankrupt. In the future, we can only rely on insurance to remedy the situation.

Central Bank Takes Over the Customs Tax Collection Office

▲Ren Li Tisheng as Director...Shen Fu as Deputy Director

The Jianghai Customs Tax Collection Office was previously managed by the Bank of China, but as a national tax agency, it was changed to joint management by the Central Bank and the Bank of China last year. The two banks each dispatched staff to manage the affairs and set a deadline. Now that the deadline has expired, it should be taken back and managed by the Central Bank itself. Therefore, on the day before yesterday (the 4th), Li Tisheng was appointed as the director of the office, and Shen Fu was appointed as the deputy director (stationed at the office). They have both arrived at the office to assume their duties. Yesterday, they met with the staff and encouraged them to continue working as usual. It is also heard that more than ten new staff members will be added.

Jiangsu Province's Regulations on Business Tax

▲National Federation of Chambers of Commerce Telegraphs Request for Correction

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating that on January 21 of this year, they received Decree No. 5493 from the Ministry, which forwarded the Outline of Business Tax and supplementary measures, requesting that they be circulated and notified. The telegram stated that the nine articles of the Business Tax Outline are quite inconsistent with the resolutions of the National Internal Tax Reduction Conference in July of the 17th year of the Republic of China, and the Business Tax Regulations and Implementation Rules formulated by Jiangsu Province are even more contrary to the Outline. The Federation has repeatedly received inquiries from various chambers of commerce and has been unable to answer. It is appropriate to telegraph to the Ministry, based on the intention of reducing internal taxes to save the people, to promptly correct the tax regulations formulated by Jiangsu Province, so as to relieve the suffering of Jiangsu merchants and dispel public doubts. The telegraph was signed by Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce.

City Chamber of Commerce Answers Various Questions About Business Tax

The City Chamber of Commerce has received inquiries from various industries regarding the business tax issue for several days. After verifying them one by one, it has replied by letter. The replies are recorded separately below:

▲Reply to the Tongshan County Chamber of Commerce: We received your letter of the 4th of this month, asking how our Chamber of Commerce expresses itself regarding the business tax matter and asking us to investigate and reply. Our Chamber of Commerce belongs to the city's scope. The business tax in our city should be implemented after being formulated by the city government. It is currently in the planning and formulation stage, and our Chamber of Commerce has been allowed to select representatives to participate in the discussion. Because our city has not suffered any losses from internal tax reduction, (internal taxes belong to national taxes, and internal tax surcharges belong to provincial taxes, so the city's finances are not affected by internal tax reduction,) and because of the relationship with the concessions, the city authorities are still carefully considering this matter, and it is not as hasty as in other provinces. As for the business tax rates set by Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, they are indeed too high and have an indirect impact on our city. Therefore, various industries have organized tax rule committees to elect representatives to go to Beijing to petition, requesting that the Ministry of Finance order the two provinces to handle the matter in accordance with the outline. The Church has also repeatedly telegraphed the Ministry of Finance to repeatedly state this matter, and the texts of the telegrams are published in various newspapers at any time. We hope you have read them.

▲Reply to the Tea Industry Association: We received your letter of the 4th of this month, asking what percentage of the business tax the various provinces have set for the tea industry and asking us to investigate and inform you. According to reports, the business tax rates in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces combine tea and lacquer into one category called tea and lacquer tax, with a tax rate of 5 per mille. The tea industry in the E province is established as a separate category and the tax rate is 2.5 per mille. We are sending this letter in response, hoping you will take note.

▲Reply to the Cosmetics Association: We received your letter of the 4th of this month, stating that the collection of business tax on cosmetics should be classified in detail according to the trademark classification method and should not be generally regarded as luxury goods. We have forwarded it to the ministry and province for adoption. The business tax is based on the industry as the unit, not on goods as the unit, such as customs duties, internal taxes, and consumption taxes. The Ministry of Finance has recently telegraphed this matter to various provinces, urging them to correct it. Therefore, your letter's proposal to further classify according to the detailed rules of goods in one industry violates the principles of business tax and the Ministry's telegram. However, we find that the business tax rates in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces list luxury goods and levy a business tax of 20 per mille. Those whose nature cannot be purely regarded as luxury goods, such as the Western medicine industry, are similar to your industry's situation. Our association is planning to organize a special committee to conduct a detailed study in order to compile a case and plan for remedies. We will wait until the overall plan is handled.

Beijing-Shanghai Railway Replacing Sleepers

In order to remedy train delays and revitalize passenger transport, the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Administration ordered six Pacific-style locomotives from the United Kingdom and has repeatedly test-driven them, inviting various Chinese and foreign circles in this city to observe and ride them. Details have been seen in previous reports. However, it is learned that the tonnage of the locomotives is heavier than the old ones, and the vibration force of the fuselage is also greater when moving. However, the sleepers currently laid on the railway are old, and the trackside spikes may loosen due to the influence of the vibration force. Therefore, the railway bureau specially purchased a large batch of sleepers from the United Kingdom and started construction at the beginning of the month, replacing them in sections. Once the replacement is completed, the new locomotives can be put into use. Last night, the railway administration specially tested the locomotives on the sections where the sleepers have been replaced.

Dr. Wu Lien-teh's Anti-Smoking Proposal

The Kwok Man Press reports that Dr. Wu Lien-teh, the Chinese representative at the 1911 League of Nations Opium Conference, recently authored an article titled "The Opium Problem, a Deeply Pernicious Influence," in which he expressed his anti-smoking views. The original text is as follows:

The problem of opium (and narcotics) has now become widespread globally, reaching an extreme point. Before 1907, it was commonly believed that only the Chinese people were addicted to this vice. Therefore, the laws concerning narcotics enacted by countries such as Britain, Portugal, the Netherlands, Japan, France, and their colonies were often lenient, but harshly criticized the Chinese people's indulgence in this harmful drug that everyone knew about. After the European War, Western countries have realized that this kind of narcotic poison has spread and infiltrated into countries claiming to be clean and upright. This is because occasional mental stimulation, temporary physical pain, casual entertainment, lingering affection between the sexes, Buddhist tranquility, and physical fatigue are all enough to lure people into becoming inseparable companions with this thing. Moreover, indulging in singing and dancing venues, indulging in pleasure late into the night, almost forgetting the east and its fish, and competing for extravagance and licentiousness, neglecting their duties, are even more likely to cause people to fall into the abyss, which is mostly in the black market. Now, let us first discuss China's recent opium problem. Since China and Britain concluded the ten-year treaty, stipulating that opium trade should be gradually reduced within the period to achieve the purpose of prohibition, the opium produced within China previously amounted to at least 400,000 piculs (each picul equals 133 pounds in British weight), half of which was produced in Sichuan and Shanxi provinces, and the rest came from India, in thousands of boxes per year (each box weighs 133 pounds), all subject to heavy taxes. However, less than three years after the signing of the treaty, thanks to the strict prohibition efforts of Governor-General Zhao Erxun and his brothers, all the fields for growing poppies were swept away. The farmers all obeyed the order to switch to growing wheat and cotton. But at this time, opium was still imported, mostly from India via Yunnan, Taiwan, Qingdao, and the Manchurian border, smuggled into the country. In 1911, the Republic of China was established. Later, in order to raise funds easily, President Yuan Shikai and warlords who held their own armies did not hesitate to relax the ban on smoking. As a result, poppy seedlings reappeared throughout the country, and they even imposed taxes in the name of collecting taxes, ignoring the public opinion against drugs, thus delaying until now for nearly 20 years, the opium ban has almost become a bubble. At the same time, school textbooks all painfully describe the harm of opium, but they are all regarded as mere formalities. The situation is similar to that before 1900. Up to now, the amount of opium produced nationwide is no less than 200,000 piculs, almost equal to half the amount of opium before the Sino-British treaty in 1907. The opium trade is protected by warlords, and the opium-producing areas are very wide. The estimated annual profit is at least 50 million to 100 million taels. However, the government has never obtained any tax revenue from this, and it is all pocketed by the operators and those who provide protection, which is a great shame to the international community. Some may ask, is there really no solution to save this situation? Or will the most practical methods based on experience be used to cater to the national anti-drug policy announced, and the huge sums of money previously pocketed by powerful people be returned to the central treasury, turning private gains into public benefits, achieving a win-win strategy? I believe that we are not necessarily at a loss. Based on my many years of heartbreaking experience, I offer some humble opinions as follows. Whether they are appropriate or not, I hope those who care about opium administration will carefully consider them: (1) The central authorities should immediately convene a concrete meeting of leaders from the industrial and scientific communities by the anti-smoking bureau established by the government to determine fundamental methods and eliminate the danger of opium poisoning; (2) Begin an accurate survey of the number of mu of poppy cultivation in each province, so that the authorities can base it on the anti-smoking policy; (3) Aim to completely ban the trade of drugs within fifteen years. During this period, the government should strictly supervise the opium produced domestically, especially paying attention to the ports and cities where raw opium enters and exits; (4) Hire experienced customs officials to handle tax collection matters. Assuming that each picul is taxed at 2,000 taels of silver, this amount should be stored separately and not mixed with other tax revenues, so that this amount can be used to handle anti-smoking affairs, so that it is not necessary to consume national currency or raise funds separately; (5) At least 10% of the total amount of this tax revenue must be used to set up smoking cessation centers, public hospitals, and other recurring expenses in various key ports, so as to help people quit smoking on the one hand, and handle anti-drug and health propaganda on the other; (6) It is necessary to carry out the above-mentioned points at the same time, strictly controlling the amount of opium planted and consumed, reducing it by 1/15 each year, so that the opium fields and opium farmers in each province can gradually reduce and eliminate opium poison according to the government's anti-smoking policy, so as to avoid difficult situations; (7) At the beginning of the implementation of the ban, it seems inappropriate to be too concerned or have complicated procedures, such as opium addicts obtaining licenses and taking photos. This procedure not only consumes a lot of administrative expenses, but also easily opens up loopholes, and it is not welcomed by those who quit smoking; (8) Some may say that the government has now clearly banned smoking, so why allow people to smoke again? Isn't this a contradiction and ridicule? In fact, it is not. Gradually correcting past mistakes is better than delaying. The United States is rich and powerful, with a perfect organization, and its population is only a quarter of China's. It has not been able to find a good solution to the alcohol prohibition problem, which can be used as a lesson. Now, let us discuss the problem of pure narcotics, such as cocaine and various opium derivatives, and the refining of other counterfeit alkaline compounds. In recent years, countries around the world have paid more attention to the harm of morphine (and cocaine) than to the opium problem. I had already considered this in 1919, and now it has invaded various countries, especially spreading rapidly in developed countries, just like the influenza epidemic, raging in civilized countries. Twenty years ago, there were only a handful of manufacturers of morphine and other narcotics, but today there are more than 140 commercial firms openly selling this harmful compound, as far as my records show. The one that has been operating for a short time but producing the most is Turkey. According to the latest report received by the League of Nations, Turkey exports 5,200 kilograms of morphine and 8,650 kilograms of heroin every year. This means that the Turkey of this new era is now manufacturing half of the world's morphine needs (a total of 12,000 kilograms) and more than the total amount of heroin the world needs (a total of 8,650 kilograms). Truly, Turkey is good at learning from advanced Europe. Recently, many fashionable young people often carry narcotics with them as a way to refresh themselves. Since the European War, the morality of commerce and professional occupations has been declining, so the sales of narcotics have been increasing day by day, and the traces of private sellers are all over the country. In major ports such as San Francisco, New York, Singapore, Yangon, Shanghai, Otsu, Hong Kong, and Marseille, large quantities of private drugs are often seized, which is enough to prove the high profits of this illegal trade, so many people flock to it. Other famous actresses, movie stars, doctors in various departments, and seemingly decent businessmen, wealthy people of unknown origin, etc., are also trading in this for profit and becoming victims of narcotics. League of Nations personnel are thinking about eliminating this evil, but they don't know what to do. This is also the retribution that European countries are eating. They thought that this drug only affected degenerate nations, and they could take advantage of it to suck their fat, lighten their burden, and hope to reap its benefits. Since the signing of the Hague Convention in 1912, all countries have agreed to ban narcotics, but year after year, all countries have regarded it as insignificant and remained silent. This is why the representatives of China and Thailand refused to sign the 1925 treaty and left the Geneva conference. The problem of narcotics is complicated and difficult. It is necessary to start early, which is not comparable to the arms reduction problem. If all countries can enthusiastically engage in it, it is not difficult to reach a fair solution. I have also made some suggestions in this regard. Fortunately, Mr. Wu Kaisheng, the representative of our country, has also made proposals at the Geneva conference. Generally, it is proposed to establish a general narcotics manufacturing plant at the location of the League of Nations and send personnel to supervise the manufacture of counterfeit alkaline compounds legally needed for medical purposes around the world. The manufacturing plants in other countries should be closed immediately. The quantity of their manufacture can be based on the number of 450 mg per person in developed medical countries determined by League of Nations experts. The factory can also be the official agency of the general administration for allocating and selling these narcotics to factories that have already been established (the fewer the types, the better). This agency can allocate them to the personnel officially appointed by each country's government to avoid abuses. A research department should also be established to conduct physiological and chemical tests on addictive drugs in order to gradually improve and achieve the goal of completely eliminating bad habits. The reasons for opposing the League of Nations' supervision of manufacturing are twofold: (1) The investment issues of countries that have always manufactured narcotics. However, if this issue involves armaments and equipment, it is indeed important and difficult to resolve. The manufacture of narcotics is a relatively new business, and it is not difficult to negotiate a liquidation method with the governments concerned. (2) The issue of national tranquility in wartime. During wartime, the medical needs for narcotics increase sharply. If they are supplied from abroad, it is not as convenient as making and using them themselves. However, this matter is not important. Once the war starts, necessities such as gasoline, kerosene, and food are even more important than narcotics. In short, the League of Nations is a detached international organization, and there will be no abuses if it supervises the manufacturing. I hope that the authorities in various countries who are blinded by the profits of narcotics will think twice and not endanger the future of world peace for their own selfish interests. Readers may think that my suggestions are revolutionary, but now is the era of creation. All scholars who are responsible for seeking world happiness should consider any reasonable plan to achieve this goal.
